  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_7daed609-0a02-496d-8012-0a931034a9df'

  <span id="freeText14821473320611540825" style="display:none">Alyss of Wonderland's rule has only just begun, and already those who prefer chaos to peace are threatening to destroy everything worth imagining. Trailed by newly appointed royal bodyguard Homburg Molly, Alyss is doing her best to keep pace with the non-stop demands of being queen while attempting to evade Molly for a few private moments with Dodge.<br /><br />Alyss' life is a challenging mix of duty, love, and tough decisions, and then a series of phantom sightings set fire to an urban myth of Her Imperial Viciousness' return and have everyone... seeing Redd.<br /><br />Has Redd somehow freed herself and her chief assassin, The Cat, from the confines of the Heart Crystal? If not, then who has resurrected Redd's brutal foot soldiers the Glass Eyes and set them loose to attack Wonderland on all sides?<br /><br />Battles rage, looking glasses explode, and the Alyssians once again unite to defend White Imagination in this fast-paced follow-up to the <i>New York Times</i> best-selling <i>The Looking Glass Wars</i>.</span>

<div id="review_133143481" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/133143481" />
    <a title="Jamie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4605519-jamie"><img alt="Jamie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1319681755p2/4605519.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/133143481?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jamie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jamie" href="/user/show/4605519-jamie">Jamie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4605519-jamie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4605519-jamie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer133143481" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5958800969572732497">This is the sequel to <a href='http://vailiapageturner.blogspot.com/2013/06/the-looking-glass-wars-review.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Looking Glass Wars</a>. <br/><br/>Redd has been banished from Wonderland. She is determined to find her way back to her world by any means necessary. Alyss is the new queen who has much to learn about ruling. And a new enemy is making his move. King Arch of Borderlands is determined to have wonderland for himself. He reeks havoc and even kidnaps Molly. <br/><br/>Once again, Frank Beddor has done am amazing job of recreating the magical realm of Wonderland. All the favorites from the last book </span>
  <span id="freeText5958800969572732497" style="display:none">This is the sequel to <a href="http://vailiapageturner.blogspot.com/2013/06/the-looking-glass-wars-review.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Looking Glass Wars</a>. <br /><br />Redd has been banished from Wonderland. She is determined to find her way back to her world by any means necessary. Alyss is the new queen who has much to learn about ruling. And a new enemy is making his move. King Arch of Borderlands is determined to have wonderland for himself. He reeks havoc and even kidnaps Molly. <br /><br />Once again, Frank Beddor has done am amazing job of recreating the magical realm of Wonderland. All the favorites from the last book plus some new faces. Hatter continues to remain my favorite character of the story. We get a lot of insight on Redd and learn a lot about Arch. We also make progress getting to know Molly and Dodge. However, I feel as though Alyss was a bit stagnant in this volume.<br /><br />Seeing Redd is darker than the last. The villains are nastier than before, and smarter. The book also plays on a more political playing field at times. A full scale war involving the Caterpillars, Wonderlanders, Borderlanders, and men of earth clash in this next installment to the series.<br /><br />Again, I loved the character growth and backround information we get here. There were a few dull moments in the book where the pace seems to die off briefly but is quickly back to normal. Overall, a very enjoyable, magical adventure for any with Imagination!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5958800969572732497" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_85656051" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/85656051" />
    <a title="Heather" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2615211-heather"><img alt="Heather" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1265909675p2/2615211.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/85656051?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather" href="/user/show/2615211-heather">Heather</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2615211-heather?shelf=my-scifi-pics">my-scifi-pics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer85656051" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3759752963256908254">I liked The Looking Glass Wars enough to really want to like this sequel, as well. But unfortunately, all of Beddor's flaws in book 1 are even more present in Seeing Redd.<br/><br/>In this sequel, Alyss Heart is now queen of Wonderland, but she's got her hands full -- King Arch in neighboring Boarderland is plotting against her and has kidnapped Homburg Molly. Redd and her assassin The Cat have escaped to earth through the Crystal (by means not fully explained) where they're wreaking havoc and amassing an</span>
  <span id="freeText3759752963256908254" style="display:none">I liked The Looking Glass Wars enough to really want to like this sequel, as well. But unfortunately, all of Beddor's flaws in book 1 are even more present in Seeing Redd.<br /><br />In this sequel, Alyss Heart is now queen of Wonderland, but she's got her hands full -- King Arch in neighboring Boarderland is plotting against her and has kidnapped Homburg Molly. Redd and her assassin The Cat have escaped to earth through the Crystal (by means not fully explained) where they're wreaking havoc and amassing an army. Hatter Madigan stumbles on some very personal secrets and sets about to make amends. And Dodge and Alyss struggle with balancing her responsibilities, his bitterness, and their respective obligations while admitting their affections for each other.<br /><br />All of these plot twists have the making for an excellent story -- I was thrilled to see more time given to Hatter especially -- but it fell short, again, in poorly executed descriptions. There was SO much time given to Redd and Arch, and so much less to Alyss and her allies, which wouldn't have been so bad if that time had covered something interesting. But Arch and Redd are shallow, textbook villains, spouting ridiculously corny lines and plotting in predictable ways (for a truly excellent spoof of this fantasy pitfall, check out Joss Whedon's Dr. Horrible's Sing Along Blog). And when we do see the good guys, the storyline is a bit of a mess. Homburg Molly, who was endearing in book 1 because of her pluck and verve, is reduced to a zero-action existence as a captive in Arch's encampment. Hatter's big discovery and subsequent reunions and interactions around it don't really go anywhere exciting (I can't say more without giving away plot, but after all the build-up about his deep, hidden emotions, the actual fell pretty flat). Dodge and Alyss start some interesting conversations about what it means to love and protect someone against their own self-hatred and bitterness, but again, the theme is left undeveloped while the plot turns to repeated vague descriptions of combat. I still don't know what a spirit-dane is, although thankfully I could actually read the map in book 2. And when will that rook be given an actual name???<br /><br />But I admit, I'll tough this out for book 3, simply because the story is creative, and hope Beddor improves. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3759752963256908254" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sammi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sammi" href="/user/show/1736691-sammi">Sammi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer48273423" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16450374508120489318">I am not going to lie, I liked this book much better than the first. Something about it was so much more interesting, so indefinably more plot oriented, that I just couldn't help but like it more.<br/>By the way, Hatter Madigan is still the bomb.<br/>One of the reasons I think I like t so much better is because of Redd. She is just such a good villain, cruel, merciless...everything a good reader could want. I find nothing more enjoyable than a bad guy who thinks everything else is below them. It's an odd </span>
  <span id="freeText16450374508120489318" style="display:none">I am not going to lie, I liked this book much better than the first. Something about it was so much more interesting, so indefinably more plot oriented, that I just couldn't help but like it more.<br />By the way, Hatter Madigan is still the bomb.<br />One of the reasons I think I like t so much better is because of Redd. She is just such a good villain, cruel, merciless...everything a good reader could want. I find nothing more enjoyable than a bad guy who thinks everything else is below them. It's an odd characteristic to be sure, but the better the antagonist is, the more interesting the book will be, since the main character(s) will have to work that much harder to defeat him or her.<br />I also enjoyed King Arch's position in the story. He pulled strings and made me want to yell at the main characters for not suspecting him (another good quality in a well made villain, though of course he was no match for Redd). Also, his extremely sexist attitude, though annoying, made his character so different from many fantasy kings. Usually in a world such as this, the author eliminates sexist attitudes because the women have so much to offer. Not Arch. He looks down at women, even after having Redd as his neighbor for thirteen years. It is amusing, in a way, how this stupidity both defines and weakens his character.<br />The good guys as well were marginally more interesting this time around. Alyss, Dodge, Molly (though I really wish we had gotten to see more of her); even Bibwit seemed like a little less of a snob. It was excellent.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16450374508120489318" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText8302608154101401025" style="display:none">I didn't like this book as much as the first, in large part because it feels almost like a place holder to get everyone back in the game before the final confrontation. <div id="review_21785308" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/21785308" />
    <a title="Chris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1124585-chris"><img alt="Chris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1209425909p2/1124585.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/21785308?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris" href="/user/show/1124585-chris">Chris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124585-chris?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21785308" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17271113727098905134">Ah, Alyss and Wonderland. I first jumped down Beddor's rabbit hole with the <i>Hatter M</i> comics and shortly after that with <i>The Looking Glass Wars</i>. I had just finished reading the 'original' Alice stories by Carroll and had that imagery fresh in my head. I thoroughly enjoyed the first book and had a lot of fun with the new and very creative interpretation of the Wonderland world and the characters and interactions found there. Snippets of Beddor's writing style bugged me a little bit, but I got used</span>
  <span id="freeText17271113727098905134" style="display:none">Ah, Alyss and Wonderland. I first jumped down Beddor's rabbit hole with the <i>Hatter M</i> comics and shortly after that with <i>The Looking Glass Wars</i>. I had just finished reading the 'original' Alice stories by Carroll and had that imagery fresh in my head. I thoroughly enjoyed the first book and had a lot of fun with the new and very creative interpretation of the Wonderland world and the characters and interactions found there. Snippets of Beddor's writing style bugged me a little bit, but I got used to them.<br /><br />In <i>Seeing Redd</i>, the second book in the Looking Glass saga, I wasn't quite as happily fulfilled. The first book, while it had a handful of issues like most books do, was a tightly woven story with compelling characters and a great story arc. While it obviously left itself open for the potential of a continuing saga, it also tied up most loose ends and left us with a very fulfilling and happy place to leave Alyss and her friends. The second book did not tie things up neatly. Normally that wouldn't be a problem for me. Some of my favorite books have been members of a series and often ended with wildly dramatic cliffhangers. <br /><br />So what is different about Seeing Redd that leaves me unhappily unsettled? The problem, as I see it, is that the tone and styling of the novel seemed almost ignorant to the fact that it was leaving so much in the air by its end. The writing seemed to believe that everything was going to tie itself off nicely by the end of the final page. Rather than identifying and exposing the suspense of the loose threads, the novel practically disavowed their existence.<br /><br />In the first book, I found myself turning pages faster and faster as I neared the end and as I did so, I was growing more and more nervous that the author wasn't going to have time to wrap things up. In the first book, the action took on a rip-roaring pace to finish things up neatly in a short amount of time. It moved quickly but didn't become disorienting.<br /><br />As I neared the end of book two, I was again nervous that things weren't going to wrap up, but I recalled my previous experience and trusted the author to leave me with a satisfactory ending because I had no suggestions from the text that there would be any sort of suspenseful interlude between book 2 and book 3.<br /><br />As the climax of the final battle wound down, I realized that I was in fact going to have to wait until book 3 for any additional conclusion. I wasn't left with a cliffhanger or any sort of major suspense. Rather, the resulting finish left me in a state of confusion. Most of the major action of book 2 had been nullified completely. There were a few alliances made which could be utilized in future stories. There were some intriguing actions that needed to be re-explored (like the kidnapping of a certain author), but for the most part, I feel like I could probably jump right into book 3 without ever reading book 2 and it's not likely that I would miss anything that a single chapter couldn't recap (<i>"Character X aligns with Character Y. Characters A and B are betrayed and killed by Character X.", etc.</i>).<br /><br />Still, I am absolutely enjoying this world and the stories and imagination in this new Wonderland. I look forward to the new adventures. Despite my complaints above, I truly did enjoy this book and had a lot of fun with the characters and their struggles and triumphs. I just would have preferred the book to either be more adept in 'wrapping things up' or in adequately portraying a sense of suspense and anticipation for things to come. The current ending left me in a bit of a stupor.<br /><br />***<br />2 1/2 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="17271113727098905134" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_999801154" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/999801154" />
    <a title="Jane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9706360-jane"><img alt="Jane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537650759p2/9706360.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/999801154?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jane" href="/user/show/9706360-jane">Jane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142412091" href="/book/show/2801635-seeing-redd">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer999801154" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11154229163814223452">I honestly didn't care that much for the first book in this series. I read this because I'm honestly just trying to power through a pile of books I've obtained over the span of a few years, so my expectations were pretty low for this novel.<br/><br/>Like the first installment, the writing in this book is about a middle school level (think Stephanie Meyer). The whole, it felt like I was reading poorly written fanfiction (and there are some great, well-written fanfiction out there!). The characters were ver</span>
  <span id="freeText11154229163814223452" style="display:none">I honestly didn't care that much for the first book in this series. I read this because I'm honestly just trying to power through a pile of books I've obtained over the span of a few years, so my expectations were pretty low for this novel.<br /><br />Like the first installment, the writing in this book is about a middle school level (think Stephanie Meyer). The whole, it felt like I was reading poorly written fanfiction (and there are some great, well-written fanfiction out there!). The characters were very flat and lifeless, the relationships forced and predictable. It honestly reads more like a script for a graphic novel, with the amount of obnoxious text sound effects. That format would better suited to the story for a lot of writings, poor writing being first and foremost. <br /><br />As far as the plot goes, the author has some pretty interesting ideas but is terrible at executing them. Some of the concepts of Wonderland and the characters were pretty interesting but just weren't given enough time to develop into something better. King Arch for example. Terribly sexist, awful ruler. He literally sounded like a ten year old who didn't like girls, plain and simple. Instead of using his sexism as a kind of talking point, to illustrate how that shows him as a weaker ruler, etc, he just makes royal decrees that men can't cry or watch rom-coms, basically. Think the MRA skit with Lena Dunham on SNL, another interesting idea that went nowhere.<br /><br />My other complaint would be the magic. I'm totally fine with magic that doesn't have a lot of rules or explanation to it, but the imagination didn't really make sense at all. Another reviewer mentioned that Alyss and Redd seemed to just be doing the same thing over and over, and I agree. It wasn't particularly impressive, imaginative, or unique in it's powers and how Wonderlanders used them. <br /><br />Again, I definitely did not read this book because I had any kind of hope for it, I fully expected to not like it. For anyone who loves Wonderland and all of it's new and different incarnations, I would recommend this book for it's IDEAS but caution strongly against the writing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11154229163814223452" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12028811052132983702">So...I was not too sure about the first book of this series. I like the idea and concept however the writing was a little bad in some ways and was a bit off-putting. I read Seeing Redd in an attempt to pursue the storyline more than my enjoyment of the first book. <br/><br/>I think Beddor got a little in over his head with this one.   <span id="freeText12028811052132983702" style="display:none">So...I was not too sure about the first book of this series. I like the idea and concept however the writing was a little bad in some ways and was a bit off-putting. I read Seeing Redd in an attempt to pursue the storyline more than my enjoyment of the first book. <br /><br />I think Beddor got a little in over his head with this one. The plot is as follows:<br />After the end of the first book, Redd has jumped into the Crystal Heart, so we aren't sure if she is dead or alive and plotting, meanwhile Arch the king of lands outside of Wonderland is plotting to take over Alyss' queendom by his own means.<br /><br />Where I think that this book went nuts was that the book really doesn't have an ending, nothing gets resolved, you are left on a complete and total cliff when it comes to the overall plot line...meaning you HAVE to read the 3rd book.<br /><br />At this point I have no intention of reading the next one, the writing in book 2 much like book 1 was pretty bad, and seemed a little word vomit-y (everything that came to mind was immediately written and then left be). While I am interested in the plot ending and to see if Alyss lives happily ever after, I am not willing to take up any more of my time at the moment.</span>

<div id="review_907152540" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/907152540" />
    <a title="Mizuki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki"><img alt="Mizuki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368277474p2/16842102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

<div id="review_3200870146" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3200870146" />
    <a title="Carrie (brightbeautifulthings)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9868179-carrie-brightbeautifulthings"><img alt="Carrie (brightbeautifulthings)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1491349112p2/9868179.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3200870146?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carrie (brightbeautifulthings)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carrie (brightbeautifulthings)" href="/user/show/9868179-carrie-brightbeautifulthings">Carrie (brightbeautifulthings)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9868179-carrie-brightbeautifulthings?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9868179-carrie-brightbeautifulthings?shelf=go-ask-alice">go-ask-alice</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9868179-carrie-brightbeautifulthings?shelf=fairytale-retellings">fairytale-retellings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3200870146" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12567571841566714171">There are spoilers ahead for The Looking Glass Wars. Alyss Heart is the newly instated queen of Wonderland, but the threats haven’t stopped since Redd jumped into the Heart Crystal. She worries her aunt will appear in another form, and she’s facing threats from Boarderland’s misogynistic King Arch. When there’s an attack on the Crystal Continuum and her personal bodyguard, Homburg Molly, goes missing, Alyss’s queendom is threatened from within. Hatter Madigan will do anything to get Molly back i</span>
  <span id="freeText12567571841566714171" style="display:none">There are spoilers ahead for The Looking Glass Wars. Alyss Heart is the newly instated queen of Wonderland, but the threats haven’t stopped since Redd jumped into the Heart Crystal. She worries her aunt will appear in another form, and she’s facing threats from Boarderland’s misogynistic King Arch. When there’s an attack on the Crystal Continuum and her personal bodyguard, Homburg Molly, goes missing, Alyss’s queendom is threatened from within. Hatter Madigan will do anything to get Molly back including, even, disobeying his queen. Threats: death, parent death, some people being eaten alive, violence, blood, raging sexism and bigotry from the villain, fat-shaming, grief.<br /><br />Sometimes my feelings about a series don’t change that much throughout, and Seeing Redd is about on the same level as The Looking Glass Wars. The things I liked about it are consistent: solid characters, imaginative world-building, rapid pace. The things I didn’t are the same: uninspiring villains, not quite enough descriptions of all the weird magic and weapons. There are maybe a few too many action scenes here, as almost every chapter includes a battle of some kind, and an overdose of sound effects. I started skipping everything in italics, since I’m reading a novel and not a comic book.<br /><br />This also scales back the character development quite a bit, and I didn’t see as much of Alyss coming into her power as I wanted to in this book. If anyone has development, it’s Hatter, and it’s easy to see that Beddor is more enamored of his stoic assassin than his Wonderland queen. (There’s also at least one character in here that serves no purpose whatsoever, except perhaps additional angst.) I don’t know that Arch is a better villain than Redd, but I certainly had more feelings about him, and they were all bad. The man can’t say a word without offending the entire female species, and I look forward to the day Redd double crosses him and feeds him to her flesh-eating roses.<br /><br />Seeing Redd also has the slight lull of second books in a trilogy. It sets up its own plot with renewed threats on Wonderland from Redd and its neighboring kingdom, Boarderland, but almost all of the closure is left for the third novel. While I like the characters and the world-building, the overall plot isn’t all that different from a lot of fantasy and dystopian trilogies. Our heroes are fighting to overthrow an oppressive ruler and defend their king (or queen)dom. While books like this might have been setting the trend for that plot ten years ago, it’s not one of my favorite stories. I like these, but I’ll probably never love them.<br /><br />I review regularly at brightbeautifulthings.tumblr.com.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12567571841566714171" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6897341614323050953">In the author's Biography in the back of the book, it says that Frank Beddor is currently writing a screenplay for this series to be made into movies. What wasn't mentioned is that he practically already has. This book is just a movie in book form. It has all the blockbuster essentials: cheesy lines, ridiculously long action and battles, conflicted, attractive characters. You know. "Dodge held his Alyss's face in his hands, wiping of her tears with his thumbs..." "Did you lose something? *chops </span>
  <span id="freeText6897341614323050953" style="display:none">In the author's Biography in the back of the book, it says that Frank Beddor is currently writing a screenplay for this series to be made into movies. What wasn't mentioned is that he practically already has. This book is just a movie in book form. It has all the blockbuster essentials: cheesy lines, ridiculously long action and battles, conflicted, attractive characters. You know. "Dodge held his Alyss's face in his hands, wiping of her tears with his thumbs..." "Did you lose something? *chops of robot's head* 'cause I think I see your head over there!" You know it. <br /><br />Not to say I didn't enjoy reading it, as far as enjoyment in that can go. It's a summer trash read! I wasn't expecting much, which is always good to go at. <br /><br />So, despite the fact that Frank Beddor is so obviously trying to create a rabid fan base and huge world for his books before he eventually produces the movie so that he can make lots o money, it's a fun read. <br /></span>

<div id="review_251449601" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/251449601" />
    <a title="Donna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2465264-donna"><img alt="Donna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1503933667p2/2465264.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/251449601?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donna" href="/user/show/2465264-donna">Donna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2465264-donna?shelf=best-bitten">best-bitten</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2465264-donna?shelf=squeemers">squeemers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2465264-donna?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2465264-donna?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2465264-donna?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2465264-donna?shelf=re-telling">re-telling</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer251449601" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4427921441198854317"><b>How did we end up here?</b><br/><br/>I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/96446416' rel='nofollow noopener'>THE LOOKING GLASS WARS</a>, promptly fell in love with it and set myself on buying the next book in the series. That was a bit after I read the book and then SEEING REDD sat on my shelf for a while, getting lost in all of the other books around it. Until recently when I unearthed it and declared that I must read it for the good of my brain! My brain, it’s still thanking me.<br/> <br/><b>Okay, book. You've got 50 pages. Go!</b><br/> <br/>Just fifty? Chomp. Done.<br/><br/>It had been a while since I’ve read </span>
  <span id="freeText4427921441198854317" style="display:none"><b>How did we end up here?</b><br /><br />I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/96446416" rel="nofollow noopener">THE LOOKING GLASS WARS</a>, promptly fell in love with it and set myself on buying the next book in the series. That was a bit after I read the book and then SEEING REDD sat on my shelf for a while, getting lost in all of the other books around it. Until recently when I unearthed it and declared that I must read it for the good of my brain! My brain, it’s still thanking me.<br /> <br /><b>Okay, book. You've got 50 pages. Go!</b><br /> <br />Just fifty? Chomp. Done.<br /><br />It had been a while since I’ve read THE LOOKING GLASS WARS but as soon as I started reading Beddor’s voice came roaring back, the world popped up in Technicolor and Dolby surround sound and I was back in the game. Without missing a beat the story carried on with very little recap, something I LOVE because if you want a recap re-read the last book. Not hard. I did think Alyss was younger but she’s 20, making this series YA by . . . writing style, I guess? I don’t see anything else that’s really young adult about it except that.<br /><br />Really what it’s done is spun this old story on its head and given it new life, re-imagining this world as something both fantastical and steampunk yet still keeping a leg in an older Earth that we still know about. And let’s not forget the hint of sci-fi inherent in the other worlds being spoken about. At least that’s what I consider sci-fi. Others may not.<br /> <br /><b>What worked . . .</b><br /> <br />Everything. The three-dimensional world, the characters playing out like actors in my head, the drama going on between different groups of people, this re-imagined fairy tale come to life. What’s not to love?<br /><br />That’s not really helpful, is it?<br /> <br /><b>What didn't work . . .</b><br /> <br />As much as I was immersed in the story it was dragged on rather long only to have it come to an abrupt halt at the end, leaving a rather obvious segue into the final book but aside from being slightly irksome it’s not like that bothered me a lot.<br /><br />What I did find to get a little grating by the end was the insertion of action noises into fight scenes. Cute and quirky to start ended up being detracting from the scene by the end of it. Sets up a voice and makes the telling of it all unique but I think that kind of thing is better left for comic books than actual books. Despite the annoyance Beddor set it up so that it did fit in with everything else. It’s not like they were forced and stuck out like snapping roses or anything. It just got a little annoying reading them.<br /> <br /><b>And in the end . . .</b><br /> <br />Why don’t I have book three yet? Or any of the Hatter M books? And thankfully I was not left wanting for Hatter in SEEING REDD. I would have been one cranky woman had that happened. A strongly-worded letter may have been in order if that were the case.<br /><br />As far as sequels go, while SEEING REDD was definitely a bridge book to the final installment I still loved rolling around in Beddor’s world, watching how he bastardized Carroll’s imagination into something so much more, something richer and darker and deeper than I think Carroll ever imagined. I seriously can’t get enough of these books. Few books leave me with a loss of words and drooling for the next one. SEEING REDD was one of those books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4427921441198854317" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1392054177" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1392054177" />
    <a title="Bridget" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16022915-bridget"><img alt="Bridget" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587937178p2/16022915.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1392054177?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bridget" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bridget" href="/user/show/16022915-bridget">Bridget</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781405209885" href="/book/show/1927039.Seeing_Redd">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1392054177" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7576322829685103407">This book could have gone one of two ways: 1) it could have improved upon the issues of The Looking Glass Wars and risen to be something really spectacular, or 2) it could have deepened the issues of the first book into something really flat and empty. Guess which route Seeing Redd went down?<br/><br/>The issues I had with this sequel were basically endless. The plot was half baked, the characters were soulless and the writing was painfully mediocre, which led to an emotionless novel that I skim-read for </span>
  <span id="freeText7576322829685103407" style="display:none">This book could have gone one of two ways: 1) it could have improved upon the issues of The Looking Glass Wars and risen to be something really spectacular, or 2) it could have deepened the issues of the first book into something really flat and empty. Guess which route Seeing Redd went down?<br /><br />The issues I had with this sequel were basically endless. The plot was half baked, the characters were soulless and the writing was painfully mediocre, which led to an emotionless novel that I skim-read for the last hundred pages. <br /><br />The thing about Beddor is that he does have good ideas - however, he doesn't seem to be able to do anything with them. While there was a basic premise and some tentative gestures at some character arcs, the ground between points A and B was somehow very vague. I felt like I just got handwaved past the important stuff and directed towards a chain of action sequences that, thanks to the handwaving, didn't feel that urgent. I just wish there had been more to it, because what hints of worldbuilding and such I got seemed pretty complex. It was so frustrating to keep getting interested and then have the scene change before any real exposition happened.<br /><br />And dear god, the characters. Anyone that I felt even the slightest affection for in book one felt like a cardboard cut out of themselves in Seeing Redd. Which is saying something, because I didn't think The Looking Glass Wars had all that much characterisation to boast about either. All of their emotional progress was cut short by unconvincing dialogue and all of their actions felt wooden. Like, the most defining feature of Molly was her bloody hat, which she didn't even WEAR for most of the novel. The result was that I just couldn't engage with any of them at all, and the less said about Beddor's villains, the better. They were basically a singular stereotypical Bad Guy trope that had been stuffed into a body and made to sing.<br /><br />What really highlighted all of this was the writing. From the telling not showing, to the in-text sound effects that let Beddor get away without describing key moments of action and emotion (real example: WUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUMMMMMP!!!), this novel just read like it was trying to be a screenplay because the style was so empty.<br /><br />Overall, I was very disappointed by this book. I'm giving it two stars because it wasn't The Worst Book Ever, but I really don't know if I can be bothered to force myself through the last book in the trilogy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7576322829685103407" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_32683541" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/32683541?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Wardrip" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Wardrip" href="/user/show/1125613-jennifer-wardrip">Jennifer Wardrip</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=read-by-other-reviewers">read-by-other-reviewers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=trt-posted-reviews">trt-posted-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer32683541" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10238846576888963453">Reviewed by Breanna F. for TeensReadToo.com<br/><br/>SEEING REDD, the second book in THE LOOKING GLASS WARS series, continues off from where the last book ended. <br/><br/>Twenty-year-old Alyss is now queen of Wonderland. Her aunt, Redd, has disappeared into the Heart Crystal along with her sidekick, The Cat, and everything is starting to calm down. <br/><br/>But soon glass eyes start appearing out of nowhere and causing mayhem. Everyone believes that Redd has somehow come back and that they're all doomed. Little do they kno</span>
  <span id="freeText10238846576888963453" style="display:none">Reviewed by Breanna F. for TeensReadToo.com<br /><br />SEEING REDD, the second book in THE LOOKING GLASS WARS series, continues off from where the last book ended. <br /><br />Twenty-year-old Alyss is now queen of Wonderland. Her aunt, Redd, has disappeared into the Heart Crystal along with her sidekick, The Cat, and everything is starting to calm down. <br /><br />But soon glass eyes start appearing out of nowhere and causing mayhem. Everyone believes that Redd has somehow come back and that they're all doomed. Little do they know that these aren't Redd's glass eyes. Someone else is having them made. And that someone else is the King of Boarderland, Arch. <br /><br />King Arch has plans to take down Wonderland and all of the surrounding cities. And he is determined to do so. He has Molly (the Queen's bodyguard) captured and intends to have her father, Hatter Madigan, come rescue her. <br /><br />Meanwhile, Redd and The Cat find their way to Earth and Redd gets a whole new group of followers. She is determined to get back to Wonderland and kill Alyss so she will finally be Queen. <br /><br />Alyss and Dodge come to terms with the fact that they are meant to be together. But Dodge is still set on killing the beast that killed his parents. Nothing will get in his way -- besides Alyss, that is. <br /><br />Wonderland is in a world of trouble with King Arch and Redd doing all they can to finally get Alyss out of the picture once and for all. <br /><br />Full of violence and mayhem, SEEING REDD is an intense read. It's a pretty good second book to the series; parts were a bit slow but, overall, it was a good read. I definitely liked THE LOOKING GLASS WARS much better; for some reason it didn't seem as wordy as SEEING REDD. But this was still a good book. I especially liked the way it ended, and it should definitely be read by those who enjoyed the first book in the series. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10238846576888963453" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_99931641" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/99931641" />
    <a title="Bry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1360862-bry"><img alt="Bry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589172666p2/1360862.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/99931641?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bry" href="/user/show/1360862-bry">Bry</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780545023870" href="/book/show/507447.Seeing_Redd">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1360862-bry?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1360862-bry?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1360862-bry?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1360862-bry?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1360862-bry?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer99931641" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8172139871408216489">Listening to the audiobook on this one and really enjoying the man's voice who is doing the reading. They added in lots of effects for the different characters which is fun, and makes it really easy to distinguish who is speaking. <br/><br/>Well this book was certainly not as good as the first book. It wasn't bad, just a bit disappointing. The entire time I was reading I was like what are these people thinking? Why can't they just talk to one another, be a bit honest. If they would they would have so many</span>
  <span id="freeText8172139871408216489" style="display:none">Listening to the audiobook on this one and really enjoying the man's voice who is doing the reading. They added in lots of effects for the different characters which is fun, and makes it really easy to distinguish who is speaking. <br /><br />Well this book was certainly not as good as the first book. It wasn't bad, just a bit disappointing. The entire time I was reading I was like what are these people thinking? Why can't they just talk to one another, be a bit honest. If they would they would have so many less problems.<br /><br />The writing is very visually driven. The landscapes, weapons, etc are extremely vivid and well described, but it also means whenever something necessary to the plot occurs there is a major shift in the writing. It almost reads like a screenplay. You are going along getting all these wonderful descriptions, then its dialog-dialog-dialog, then back to descriptions. And the segways are not often subtle.<br /><br />Also, I am not all that interested in the characters. For instance, this book gave major insight into the character of Hatter Madigan, but instead of endearing him to me I was more annoyed at what led to the situation. Furthermore, I don't even have much of an interest in the main characters. Alyss is very much 'the Queen'. In the first book she was interesting with her conflicting internal emotions. Was she a child, a Queen, a rebel, or a simple Earth girl? This book she is a Queen and nothing else. They try to hint at that else with her feeling for Dodge but they didn't seem very genuine. She was basically as stiff as a bored. Even Redd who was so awesome in the first book seems more boring this book. It's almost as if she went a bit soft in this book.<br /><br />I will definitely read the 3rd book in the trilogy to determine what happens from this giant mess Beddor has created in their world, but I am not sure I will be impressed. <br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="8172139871408216489" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_259678421" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/259678421" />
    <a title="Stephanie (ShyNotebooks)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5864205-stephanie-shynotebooks"><img alt="Stephanie (ShyNotebooks)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551803316p2/5864205.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/259678421?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephanie (ShyNotebooks)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephanie (ShyNotebooks)" href="/user/show/5864205-stephanie-shynotebooks">Stephanie (ShyNotebooks)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5864205-stephanie-shynotebooks?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer259678421" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16976607795730243908">Sorry to say, this book was far less interesting than the last one. I know, right, what happened?<br/><br/>The pacing was actually slower. I guess. Maybe I was just less interested. In the last book, I was rushing to the end because I wanted Alyss to be reunited with Dodge + Friends. In this book, Alyss was just kind of depressing, and her relationship with Dodge was more of a...competition? Sort of? I'll think of a better word later, but they pretty much sucked romance out of the whole thing. To be hones</span>
  <span id="freeText16976607795730243908" style="display:none">Sorry to say, this book was far less interesting than the last one. I know, right, what happened?<br /><br />The pacing was actually slower. I guess. Maybe I was just less interested. In the last book, I was rushing to the end because I wanted Alyss to be reunited with Dodge + Friends. In this book, Alyss was just kind of depressing, and her relationship with Dodge was more of a...competition? Sort of? I'll think of a better word later, but they pretty much sucked romance out of the whole thing. To be honest, I don't even remember much of Alyss at all in this book. It basically toggled between Hatter and Redd. <br /><br />Also, I might just be cold hearted, but I had already placed Hatter Madigan on my Shelf of Epic Warriors along with, say, Batman, (which is a big freaking deal!) and here he goes and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[has a family <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Makes him less epic. I'm sorry, it's the truth! This is why the last Superman movie sucked, amongst other reasons. And since his storyline is at least half the plot, you can see why I wasn't that intrigued. <br /><br />Sidenote: Weaver and Molly are the most annoying names in the history of bookdom. I don't know why. They just rub me the wrong way. I'm sure there are others, like...Piper (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7624272.The_Lost_Hero__Heroes_of_Olympus___1_" title="The Lost Hero (Heroes of Olympus, #1) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lost Hero</a>). That's a dumb one too. I'm going on a rabbit trail now...<br /><br />Like I said, other people might think that Hatter's part of the story was fantastic and heart-warming, blah blah. Just not my thing. <br /><br />And then Redd was just annoying. She's like...a brat that I'd like to slap. And sadly, I was in her head a lot thanks to the way the narration was structured. <br /><br />So, unfortunately, almost all of the characters disappointed me in this book. I'll read the next one because I might as well finish the series. It's quick enough. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16976607795730243908" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_72928939" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/72928939" />
    <a title="Lexie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/712966-lexie"><img alt="Lexie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478802017p2/712966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/72928939?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lexie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lexie" href="/user/show/712966-lexie">Lexie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/712966-lexie?shelf=autographed">autographed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/712966-lexie?shelf=books-once-owned">books-once-owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/712966-lexie?shelf=review-blog-pr">review-blog-pr</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer72928939" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9512211764116224993">The second book in Beddor's Looking Glass Wars trilogy picks up fairly closely to the end of the first book. 3 lunar cycles (I'm guessing this means months) later and Queen Alyss is doing her best to reassure the people that White Imagination is once again dominate.<br/><br/>There is a little bit of a mislead throughout the book as well, in who's actually the source of evil and motives. King Arch, briefly mentioned and shown in the first book, is a central character this time around (with all his sexist v</span>
  <span id="freeText9512211764116224993" style="display:none">The second book in Beddor's Looking Glass Wars trilogy picks up fairly closely to the end of the first book. 3 lunar cycles (I'm guessing this means months) later and Queen Alyss is doing her best to reassure the people that White Imagination is once again dominate.<br /><br />There is a little bit of a mislead throughout the book as well, in who's actually the source of evil and motives. King Arch, briefly mentioned and shown in the first book, is a central character this time around (with all his sexist views) and Jack of Diamonds, unfortunately, makes a return appearance. His parents aren't the brightest ever. Redd is more cunning then in the first book, using subterfuge as a way to win out. I admired her, despite her evilness, because she didn't just whine about what she lost (like Jack) or spout impossible ideas (like Arch), but had a solid plan which would have worked.<br /><br />Hatter Madigan, this poor guy, is put through the ringer. He did take his leave, as he said he would at the end of Book 1, and didn't plan on coming back. We learn more about the civilian he loved, Weaver and what secrets she carried. Which all relates back to Molly (I'm sure you can guess how) and has a surprising turn of events. Doesn't last long however. Molly is also put through the ringer--unsure of herself, prideful of her abilities but shamed by her birth, young and basically self-trained, Arch takes advantage of that weakness.<br /><br />In the end I enjoyed this book moreso then the first. I enjoyed learning more about the other lands surrounding Wonderland (even if Borderland is...what it is) and despite the ending leaving itself very open to a sequel, I can't be too upset over that. The conflicts of THIS book were resolved and the ending opened the door to a new conflict.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9512211764116224993" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_2038265'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2038265.Things_I_ve_Learned_from_Women_Who_ve_Dumped_Me"><img alt="Things I&#39;ve Learned from Women Who&#39;ve Dumped Me" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1430378008l/2038265._SX98_.jpg" />

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('eTdFDElPm8A7djuhxbeEgJjTooro99GkU+jC2NV70Ee2AJ8/GqTk+ddD5P6XxFRODPKzAr/t4M2XuajBwWv5Bw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4Y1Ld8Oy4ms6sRf4h6EyTB2db8b6PS9PBekb9Vbo+ZAuupFEkFmdUtaEyKfV0uKCibx+Tq0nHibBuHHsQvjQ0A==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Award-winning New York Times-bestselling author Mark Kurlansky takes us back to the food and eating habits of a younger Am<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText16442183994260507284\" style=\"display:none\">A remarkable portrait of American food before World War II, presented by the New York Times-bestselling author of Cod and Salt. Award-winning New York Times-bestselling author Mark Kurlansky takes us back to the food and eating habits of a younger America: Before the national highway system brought the country closer together; before chain restaurants imposed uniformity and low quality; and before the Frigidaire meant frozen food in mass quantities, the nation\'s food was seasonal, regional, and traditional. It helped form the distinct character, attitudes, and customs of those who ate it. In the 1930s, with the country gripped by the Great Depression and millions of Americans struggling to get by, FDR created the Federal Writers\' Project under the New Deal as a make-work program for artists and authors. A number of writers, including Zora Neale Hurston, Eudora Welty, and Nelson Algren, were dispatched all across America to chronicle the eating habits, traditions, and struggles of local people. The project, called &quot;America Eats,&quot; was abandoned in the early 1940s because of the World War and never completed. The Food of a Younger Land unearths this forgotten literary and historical treasure and brings it to exuberant life. Mark Kurlansky\'s brilliant book captures these remarkable stories, and combined with authentic recipes, anecdotes, photos, and his own musings and analysis, evokes a bygone era when Americans had never heard of fast food and the grocery superstore was a thing of the future. Kurlansky serves as a guide to this hearty and poignant look at the country\'s roots. From New York automats to Georgia Coca-Cola parties, from Arkansas possum-eating clubs to Puget Sound salmon feasts, from Choctaw funerals to South Carolina barbecues, the WPA writers found Americans in their regional niches and eating an enormous diversity of meals. From Mississippi chittlins to Indiana persimmon puddings, Maine lobsters, and Montana beavertails, they recorded the curiosities, commonalities, and communities of American food.<\/span>\n  <a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18378009-anatomies"><img alt="Anatomies: A Cultural History of the Human Body" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1393221221l/18378009._SX98_.jpg" />

<script>
//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_18378009'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18378009-anatomies?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Anatomies: A Cultural History of the Human Body<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/740196.Hugh_Aldersey_Williams?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Hugh Aldersey-Williams<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.50 avg rating &mdash; 584 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2013\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer16483839235750577039\">The human body is the most fraught and fascinating, talked-about and taboo, unique yet universal fact of our lives. It is the inspiration for art, the subject of science, and the source of some of the greatest stories ever told. In Anatomies, acclaim<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText16483839235750577039\" style=\"display:none\">The human body is the most fraught and fascinating, talked-about and taboo, unique yet universal fact of our lives. It is the inspiration for art, the subject of science, and the source of some of the greatest stories ever told. In Anatomies, acclaimed author of Periodic Tales Hugh Aldersey-Williams brings his entertaining blend of science, history, and culture to bear on this richest of subjects.\nIn an engaging narrative that ranges from ancient body art to plastic surgery today and from head to toe, Aldersey-Williams explores the corporeal mysteries that make us human: Why are some people left-handed and some blue-eyed? What is the funny bone, anyway? Why do some cultures think of the heart as the seat of our souls and passions, while others place it in the liver?\n\n\nA journalist with a knack for telling a story, Aldersey-Williams takes part in a drawing class, attends the dissection of a human body, and visits the doctor’s office and the morgue. But Anatomies draws not just on medical science and Aldersey-Williams’s reporting. It draws also on the works of philosophers, writers, and artists from throughout history. Aldersey-Williams delves into our shared cultural heritage—Shakespeare to Frankenstein, Rembrandt to 2001: A Space Odyssey—to reveal how attitudes toward the human body are as varied as human history, as he explains the origins and legacy of tattooing, shrunken heads, bloodletting, fingerprinting, X-rays, and more.\n\n\nFrom Adam’s rib to van Gogh’s ear to Einstein’s brain, Anatomies is a treasure <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8275557210211237832">Literary Sleuth and world creator Frank Beddor dared to expose the true story of Wonderland in the New York Times bestselling young adult trilogy The Looking Glass Wars. To satisfy the awakened curiosity of his readers he continued to tell the parallel adventures of Royal Bodyguard Hatter Madigan’s search for the lost princess in the graphic novel series Hatter M. He lives in Los Angeles.</span>
